	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Marks &amp; Spencer</h1>

		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"M&amp;S" redirects here. <p><b>Marks &amp; Spencer Group plc</b> (commonly abbreviated as <b>M&amp;S</b>) is a major British multinational retailer with headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Westminster,_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Westminster, London">Westminster, London</a> that specialises in selling high quality clothing, home products and food products. It is listed on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> and is a constituent of the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_250_Index" title="FTSE 250 Index">FTSE 250 Index</a>.
</p><p>M&amp;S was founded in 1884 by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Marks" title="Michael Marks">Michael Marks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Spencer_(Marks_and_Spencer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Spencer (Marks and Spencer)">Thomas Spencer</a> in <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC2000October23_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2000October23-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The company also began to sell branded goods like <a href="/wiki/Kellogg%27s_Corn_Flakes" class="mw-redirect" title="Kellogg&#39;s Corn Flakes">Kellogg's Corn Flakes</a> in November 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-top_brands_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top_brands-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> M&amp;S currently has 959 stores across the U.K. including 615 that only sell food products.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1998, the company became the first British retailer to make a pre-tax profit of over £1&#160;billion,<sup id="cite_ref-profit_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profit-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> although subsequently it went into a sudden slump, which took the company and its stakeholders by surprise. In November 2009, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Marc_Bolland" title="Marc Bolland">Marc Bolland</a>, formerly of <a href="/wiki/Morrisons" title="Morrisons">Morrisons</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> would take over as chief executive from executive chairman <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Rose" title="Stuart Rose">Stuart Rose</a> in early 2010; Rose remained in the role of non-executive chairman until he was replaced by Robert Swannell in January 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_bolland_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_bolland-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ft_bolland_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft_bolland-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In recent years, its clothing sales have fallen whilst food sales have increased after axing the <a href="/wiki/St_Michael_(brand)" title="St Michael (brand)">St. Michael</a> brand name for their own brand.
</p><p>On 22 May 2018, it was confirmed that over 100 stores will have closed by 2022 in a "radical" plan. Whether more stores will close is yet to be confirmed.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment">Establishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Establishment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_%26_Spencer,_Briggate,_Leeds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_Briggate%2C_Leeds.jpg/220px-Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_Briggate%2C_Leeds.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_Briggate%2C_Leeds.jpg/330px-Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_Briggate%2C_Leeds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_Briggate%2C_Leeds.jpg/440px-Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_Briggate%2C_Leeds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_%26_Spencer,_Briggate,_Leeds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marks and Spencer on <a href="/wiki/Briggate,_Leeds" class="mw-redirect" title="Briggate, Leeds">Briggate</a> not far from their original branch in <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The company was founded by a partnership between <a href="/wiki/Michael_Marks" title="Michael Marks">Michael Marks</a>, a <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland" title="History of the Jews in Poland">Polish Jew</a><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> from <a href="/wiki/S%C5%82onim" class="mw-redirect" title="Słonim">Słonim</a> (Marks was born into a Polish-Jewish family, a Polish refugee living in the Russian Empire, now in <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Spencer_(Marks_and_Spencer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Spencer (Marks and Spencer)">Thomas Spencer</a>, a cashier from the English market town of <a href="/wiki/Skipton" title="Skipton">Skipton</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire" title="North Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> On his arrival in England, Marks worked for a company in Leeds, called Barran, which employed refugees (see <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_Barran,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir John Barran, 1st Baronet">Sir John Barran, 1st Baronet</a>). In 1884 he met Isaac Jowitt Dewhirst while looking for work. Dewhirst lent Marks £5 which he used to establish his Penny Bazaar on <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Kirkgate_Market" title="Leeds Kirkgate Market">Kirkgate Market</a>, in Leeds.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Dewhirst also taught him a little English. Dewhirst's cashier was Tom Spencer, a bookkeeper, whose second wife, Agnes, helped improve Marks' English. In 1894, when Marks acquired a permanent stall in Leeds' covered market, he invited Spencer to become his partner.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1901 Marks moved to the <a href="/wiki/Birkenhead" title="Birkenhead">Birkenhead</a> open market where he amalgamated with Spencer. The pair were allocated stall numbers 11 &amp; 12 in the centre aisle in 1903, and there they opened the famous Penny Bazaar.  The company left Birkenhead Market on 24 February 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The next few years saw Michael Marks and Tom Spencer open market stalls in many locations around the North West of England and move the original Leeds Penny Bazaar to 20, Cheetham Hill Road, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_growth">Domestic growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Domestic growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_and_Spencer_shop,_Bekonscot.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Marks_and_Spencer_shop%2C_Bekonscot.JPG/220px-Marks_and_Spencer_shop%2C_Bekonscot.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Marks_and_Spencer_shop%2C_Bekonscot.JPG/330px-Marks_and_Spencer_shop%2C_Bekonscot.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Marks_and_Spencer_shop%2C_Bekonscot.JPG/440px-Marks_and_Spencer_shop%2C_Bekonscot.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2869" data-file-height="1966" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_and_Spencer_shop,_Bekonscot.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Representation of historic store from the 1930s, <a href="/wiki/Bekonscot" title="Bekonscot">Bekonscot</a> model village, UK</div></div></div>
<p>Marks and Spencer, known colloquially as "Marks and Sparks",<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> or "M&amp;S", made its reputation in the early 20th century with a policy of only selling British-made goods (it started to back down from this policy in the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>) It entered into long-term relationships with British manufacturers, and sold clothes and food under the "<a href="/wiki/St_Michael_(brand)" title="St Michael (brand)">St Michael</a>" brand, which was introduced in 1928. The brand honours <a href="/wiki/Michael_Marks" title="Michael Marks">Michael Marks</a>. It also accepted the return of unwanted items, giving a full cash refund if the receipt was shown, no matter how long ago the product was purchased, which was unusual for the time.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>M&amp;S staff raised £5,000 to pay for a <a href="/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">Supermarine Spitfire</a> fighter aircraft called <i>The Marksman</i> in 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 1950, virtually all goods were sold under the "St Michael" label. M&amp;S lingerie, women's clothes and girls' school uniform were branded under the "St Margaret" label until the whole range of general merchandise became "St Michael". <a href="/wiki/Simon_Marks" class="mw-redirect" title="Simon Marks">Simon Marks</a>, son of Michael Marks, died in 1964, after fifty-six years' service. <a href="/wiki/Israel_Sieff" class="mw-redirect" title="Israel Sieff">Israel Sieff</a>, the son-in-law of Michael Marks, took over as chairman and in 1968, <a href="/wiki/John_Salisse" title="John Salisse">John Salisse</a> became the company Director. A cautious international expansion began with the introduction of Asian food in 1974. M&amp;S opened stores in continental Europe in 1975 and in Ireland four years later.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The company put its main emphasis on quality, including a 1957 stocking size measuring system.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> For most of its history, it also had a reputation for offering fair value for money. When this reputation began to waver, it encountered serious difficulties. Arguably, M&amp;S has historically been an iconic retailer of 'British Quality Goods'.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The uncompromising attitude towards customer relations was summarised by the 1953 slogan: "The customer <i>is</i> always and completely right!"<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Energy efficiency was improved by the addition of thermostatically controlled refrigerators in 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>M&amp;S began selling <a href="/wiki/Christmas_cake" title="Christmas cake">Christmas cakes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christmas_pudding" title="Christmas pudding">Christmas puddings</a> in 1958. In an effort to improve the quality of their <a href="/wiki/Swiss_roll" title="Swiss roll">Swiss rolls</a>, they hired the food expert Nat Goldberg, who made a major improvement across their entire cake range, which had lost the public's favour a few years earlier. As a later measure to improve food quality, food labelling was improved and "sell by dates" were phased in between 1970 and 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Smoking was banned from all M&amp;S shops in 1959 because of the fire hazards it posed.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1972, <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Sieff,_Baron_Sieff_of_Brimpton" title="Marcus Sieff, Baron Sieff of Brimpton">Marcus Sieff</a> became chairman, remaining in place until 1984, and emphasising the importance of good staff relations to the tradition of the store,  while extending staff benefits to areas such as restaurants and chiropody.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_expansion">International expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: International expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_Tower_Marks_%26_Spencer_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Central_Tower_Marks_%26_Spencer_2009.jpg/220px-Central_Tower_Marks_%26_Spencer_2009.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Central_Tower_Marks_%26_Spencer_2009.jpg/330px-Central_Tower_Marks_%26_Spencer_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Central_Tower_Marks_%26_Spencer_2009.jpg/440px-Central_Tower_Marks_%26_Spencer_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_Tower_Marks_%26_Spencer_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Marks &amp; Spencer store in <a href="/wiki/Central,_Hong_Kong" title="Central, Hong Kong">Central, Hong Kong</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_%26_Spencer_in_Times_Square_HK_201507.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Marks_%26_Spencer_in_Times_Square_HK_201507.jpg/220px-Marks_%26_Spencer_in_Times_Square_HK_201507.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Marks_%26_Spencer_in_Times_Square_HK_201507.jpg/330px-Marks_%26_Spencer_in_Times_Square_HK_201507.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Marks_%26_Spencer_in_Times_Square_HK_201507.jpg/440px-Marks_%26_Spencer_in_Times_Square_HK_201507.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="1408" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_%26_Spencer_in_Times_Square_HK_201507.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Marks &amp; Spencer store in <a href="/wiki/Times_Square_(Hong_Kong)" title="Times Square (Hong Kong)">Times Square</a>, Causeway Bay, Hong Kong.</div></div></div>
<p>The company expanded into Canada in 1973, and at one point had forty-seven stores across Canada. Despite various efforts to improve its image, the chain was never able to move beyond its reputation there as a stodgy retailer, one that catered primarily to senior citizens and expatriate Britons. The shops in Canada were smaller than British outlets, and did not carry the same selection. In the late 1990s, further efforts were made to modernise them and also expand the customer base. Unprofitable locations were closed. Nonetheless, the Canadian operations continued to lose money, and the last 38 shops in Canada were closed in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Expansion into France began with shops opening in Paris at <a href="/wiki/Boulevard_Haussmann" title="Boulevard Haussmann">Boulevard Haussmann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a> in 1975, followed by a second Paris shop at Rosny 2 in 1977. Further expansion into other French and Belgian cities followed into the 1980s. Although the Paris shops remained popular and profitable, the Western European operation as a whole did not fare as well and eighteen shops were sold in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> However, in April 2011, M&amp;S changed directions again with an announcement to reopen a store that will not only sell clothing but food as well. In addition the group will also open several food outlets throughout the French capital. The first branch opened on 24 November 2011 at the <a href="/wiki/Champs-%C3%89lys%C3%A9es" title="Champs-Élysées">Champs-Élysées</a> in a ceremony attended by the company's CEO <a href="/wiki/Marc_Bolland" title="Marc Bolland">Marc Bolland</a>, the model <a href="/wiki/Rosie_Huntington-Whiteley" title="Rosie Huntington-Whiteley">Rosie Huntington-Whiteley</a> and the British Ambassador to France, Sir <a href="/wiki/Peter_Westmacott" title="Peter Westmacott">Peter Westmacott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1988, the company acquired <a href="/wiki/Brooks_Brothers" title="Brooks Brothers">Brooks Brothers</a>, an American clothing company<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kings_Super_Markets" class="mw-redirect" title="Kings Super Markets">Kings Super Markets</a>, a US food chain.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016 M&amp;S expanded to sell through European marketplace <a href="/wiki/Zalando" title="Zalando">Zalando</a> on their German, French, Dutch, Belgian and Austrian sites with a range of kidswear and lingerie.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_decline">Financial decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Financial decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M_%26_S,_Inverness_(1998).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/M_%26_S%2C_Inverness_%281998%29.png/220px-M_%26_S%2C_Inverness_%281998%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/M_%26_S%2C_Inverness_%281998%29.png/330px-M_%26_S%2C_Inverness_%281998%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/M_%26_S%2C_Inverness_%281998%29.png/440px-M_%26_S%2C_Inverness_%281998%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1154" data-file-height="721" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M_%26_S,_Inverness_(1998).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>M&amp;S shop in <a href="/wiki/Inverness" title="Inverness">Inverness</a> in 1998</div></div></div>
<p>M&amp;S's profits peaked in the financial year 1997/1998.<sup id="cite_ref-profit_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profit-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> At the time it was seen as a continuing success story, but with hindsight it is considered that during Sir <a href="/wiki/Richard_Greenbury" title="Richard Greenbury">Richard Greenbury</a>'s tenure as head of the company, profit margins were pushed to untenable levels, and the loyalty of its customers was seriously eroded. The rising cost of using British suppliers was also a burden, as rival retailers increasingly imported their goods from low-cost countries, but M&amp;S's belated switch to overseas suppliers undermined a core part of its appeal to the public. Another factor was the company's refusal until 2001 to accept any credit cards except its own chargecard.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>These factors combined to plunge M&amp;S into a sudden slump, which took the company, its shareholders, who included hundreds of thousands of small investors, and nearly all retail analysts and business journalists, by surprise. The company's share price fell by more than two thirds, and its profits fell from more than a billion pounds in 1997 and 1998 to £145&#160;million in the year ended 31 March 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2001, with changes in its business focus such as accepting credit cards, the introduction of the "Per Una" clothing range designed by <a href="/wiki/George_Davies_(retailer)" title="George Davies (retailer)">George Davies</a>, and a redesign of its underlying business model, profits recovered somewhat.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, M&amp;S was in the throes of an attempted takeover by <a href="/wiki/Arcadia_Group" title="Arcadia Group">Arcadia Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Home_Stores" title="British Home Stores">BHS</a> boss, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Green" title="Philip Green">Philip Green</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-green_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-green-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> On 12 July a recovery plan was announced which would involve selling off its financial services business <a href="/wiki/M%26S_Bank" title="M&amp;S Bank">M&amp;S Money</a> to <a href="/wiki/HSBC_Bank_(Europe)" title="HSBC Bank (Europe)">HSBC Bank plc</a>, buying control of the <i>Per Una</i> range, closing the <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" title="Gateshead">Gateshead</a> Lifestore and stopping the expansion of its Simply Food line of shops. <a href="/wiki/Philip_Green" title="Philip Green">Philip Green</a> withdrew his takeover bid after failing to get sufficient backing from shareholders.<sup id="cite_ref-green_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-green-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2007, M&amp;S announced the opening of the world's largest M&amp;S shop outside the UK at <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Festival_City" title="Dubai Festival City">Dubai Festival City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> On 2 October 2008, M&amp;S opened its first mainland China shop in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>. Problems with the supply chain for the first few months of opening led Stuart Rose, M&amp;S chairman, to describe failures in "basic shopkeeping".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restructuring">Restructuring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Restructuring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Twenty-two unprofitable and minor food stores, such as the ones at <a href="/wiki/Ripon" title="Ripon">Ripon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balham" title="Balham">Balham</a>, were closed in early 2009 as part of a cost cutting measure.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In August 2010, it was confirmed that the <a href="/wiki/Grantham" title="Grantham">Grantham</a> branch of M&amp;S would close, along with two other <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire" title="Lincolnshire">Lincolnshire</a> branches in <a href="/wiki/Skegness" title="Skegness">Skegness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe" title="Scunthorpe">Scunthorpe</a> due to low sales in these older format stores. The closures were met with protests from the local communities and petitions were signed in support of retaining the stores, although they went ahead.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Retail Knowledge Bank conducted an audit of the company's brands in August 2010, and revealed that sales of womenswear were at a 10-year low. The audit covered both the Limited Collection, Autograph, Autograph Weekend, Classic Collection, Per Una, Portfolio and Indigo.<sup id="cite_ref-thisismoney.co.uk_512068_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thisismoney.co.uk_512068-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <i>Draper</i> magazine claimed that Per Una was the only clothing brand not at risk of being axed while Marc Bolland considered which brands would be retained.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Per Una was planned to stay due to its successful and distinctive flair, but Portfolio and Indigo were planned to go due to poor sales.<sup id="cite_ref-thisismoney.co.uk_512068_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thisismoney.co.uk_512068-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The Limited Collection, Autograph, Autograph Weekend, and Classic Collection brands were considered for the cull during mid-2010, but were later given a reprieve.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 9 November 2010, chief executive Marc Bolland revealed plans to strengthen the company's overall brand image and targeting sales of between £800m and £1bn for which company will increase capital expenditure to £850m to £900m over the next three years to fund the plans.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters.com_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The plan also involved the discontinuation of its 'Portfolio' fashion brand and the sale of electrical products. The company also announced a new marketing strapline, 'Only at M&amp;S', and that it would revamp its website.<sup id="cite_ref-htanna_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-htanna-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bolland ordered a new store design in May 2011, and it was announced that the company would spend around £600 million between 2011 and 2014 on its UK stores, involving the launch of a range of different store formats based on the age, affluence and demographics of people in those areas. The design also included the trial of a new in-store "navigation scheme", which followed research showing that shoppers found M&amp;S store layouts confusing and "difficult to shop [in]". It also confirmed that the amount of money-off promotions and deals offered would be increased, and that it would replace the Marks &amp; Spencer label on clothing with "M&amp;S Woman" and "M&amp;S Man".<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph2_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph2-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 2013, M&amp;S's clothing division had an 11% market share in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2013 saw the launch of the <i>Best of British</i> range as well as the overhaul of <i>Per Una</i> and <i>Indigo</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-mirror1_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mirror1-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Patrick Bousquet-Chavanne became the new marketing director, succeeding Steven Sharp in July. Mark Bolland also vowed to bring "quality and style back" <sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> M&amp;S also stated it intended to increase its number of UK suppliers from the 20 it had at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-mirror1_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mirror1-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2013, it was revealed that Bill Adderley, founder of homeware chain <a href="/wiki/Dunelm_Group" title="Dunelm Group">Dunelm Group</a>, had amassed a £250m stake in M&amp;S over the past 18 months. This disclosure was made as stock market rules mean that any holding over 3 per cent share must be made public.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 January 2016 it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Marc_Bolland" title="Marc Bolland">Marc Bolland</a>, who has been CEO since 2010 would step down on 2 April 2016, and be replaced by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Rowe_(businessman)" title="Steve Rowe (businessman)">Steve Rowe</a>, head of clothing, and previously head of the food business.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_20160107_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_20160107-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2015.E2.80.9316_store_cull"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–16_store_cull">2015–16 store cull</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2015–16 store cull">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stores identified for closure in July 2015 included <a href="/wiki/Woolwich" title="Woolwich">Woolwich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walsall" title="Walsall">Walsall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erdington" title="Erdington">Erdington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aldershot" title="Aldershot">Aldershot</a> (which was there since 1922), <a href="/wiki/Pontypridd" title="Pontypridd">Pontypridd</a> in Wales, <a href="/wiki/Hounslow" title="Hounslow">Hounslow</a> in west London, and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Quays" title="Royal Quays">Royal Quays</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Shields" title="North Shields">North Shields</a>, the three full-line stores in <a href="/wiki/Stevenage" title="Stevenage">Stevenage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wood_Green" title="Wood Green">Wood Green</a> in north London, and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Dunlop" title="Fort Dunlop">The Fort shopping park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Castle_Bromwich" title="Castle Bromwich">Castle Bromwich</a> and the Simply Food in Castle Bromwich.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto2_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-newsshopper.co.uk_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsshopper.co.uk-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lewisham" title="Lewisham">Lewisham</a> store also lost a floor.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto2_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-newsshopper.co.uk_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsshopper.co.uk-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The closures in 2015 also included three traditional food and clothing shops, one Simply Food store and four Outlet stores that sell end-of-season clothing.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_48-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Some 430 workers were affected by the closures.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_48-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The cull cost up to £200m to implement; the closure included loss-making stores in European markets such as France, Belgium and the Netherlands as well as outposts in China.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_48-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto2_48-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-newsshopper.co.uk_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsshopper.co.uk-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_50-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_50-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2017.E2.80.9318_store_cull"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–18_store_cull">2017–18 store cull</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2017–18 store cull">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several were smaller stores identified for closure in November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yahoo1_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo1-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On 31 January 2018, fourteen stores were identified for closure. Stores due for closure in April included one of their oldest presences, that in the town centre of Birkenhead. Other stores due for closure, in the same month, were those in <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth" title="Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Durham,_England" title="Durham, England">Durham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fforestfach" title="Fforestfach">Fforestfach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Putney" title="Putney">Putney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Redditch" title="Redditch">Redditch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC31012018_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC31012018-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, eight other stores were earmarked for closure at a later date, pending consultation; those in <a href="/wiki/Andover,_Hampshire" title="Andover, Hampshire">Andover</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basildon" title="Basildon">Basildon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bridlington" title="Bridlington">Bridlington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falmouth,_Cornwall" title="Falmouth, Cornwall">Falmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fareham" title="Fareham">Fareham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keighley" title="Keighley">Keighley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockport" title="Stockport">Stockport</a> and an outlet store in <a href="/wiki/Denton,_Greater_Manchester" title="Denton, Greater Manchester">Denton, Greater Manchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC31012018_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC31012018-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mid_2018_store_cull">Mid 2018 store cull</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mid 2018 store cull">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 23 May 2018 M&amp;S managers confirmed that 14 more shops were to be closed and another 86 were under investigation, and thus put on notice, due to falling corporate <a href="/wiki/Sales" title="Sales">sales</a> and customer footfall levels.  This would take the total to over 100 closing by 2022,<sup id="cite_ref-yahoo.com2_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo.com2-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yahoo.com2_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo.com2-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
<sup id="cite_ref-yahoo.com1_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo.com1-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> as corporate profits plunge 62% amid sweeping store closure plans,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> which M&amp;S thought were losing money. The company hoped it would help revive profits using the corporate website.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yahoo.com2_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo.com2-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_2019_store_cull">Early 2019 store cull</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Early 2019 store cull">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 15 January 2019 the company named the next wave of 17 stores earmarked for closure. The 17 proposed closures are part of the company's five-year plan to shut more than 100 stores by 2022.  The 17 stores which it proposes to close are: Ashford, Barrow, Bedford, Boston, Buxton, Cwmbran, Deal, Felixstowe, Huddersfield, Hull, Junction One Antrim Outlet, Luton Arndale, Newark, Northwich, Rotherham, Sutton Coldfield and Weston-super-Mare.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Head_office_locations">Head office locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Head office locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paddington_Waterside_geograph-2790569-by-Colin-Smith.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Paddington_Waterside_geograph-2790569-by-Colin-Smith.jpg/220px-Paddington_Waterside_geograph-2790569-by-Colin-Smith.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Paddington_Waterside_geograph-2790569-by-Colin-Smith.jpg/330px-Paddington_Waterside_geograph-2790569-by-Colin-Smith.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Paddington_Waterside_geograph-2790569-by-Colin-Smith.jpg/440px-Paddington_Waterside_geograph-2790569-by-Colin-Smith.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="3216" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paddington_Waterside_geograph-2790569-by-Colin-Smith.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Waterside House, 35 North Wharf Road, London.</div></div></div>
<p>The headquarters of M&amp;S had been since 1957 at Michael House, <a href="/wiki/55_Baker_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="55 Baker Street">55 Baker Street</a>, London. This had formerly been the Baker Street Bazaar which had been destroyed in a fire in 1940. The site was redeveloped by M&amp;S, under the direction of the then Sir Simon Marks, as the company had outgrown its previous Bayswater HQ.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In 2004 the company moved to a new headquarters designed by <a href="/wiki/Michel_Mossessian" title="Michel Mossessian">mossessian &amp; partners</a> at Waterside House, in the new <a href="/wiki/Paddington_Basin" title="Paddington Basin">Paddington Basin</a>, London.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As well as the main offices in London, there are a number of other head office sites across the UK; Stockley Park (IT Services), <a href="/wiki/Salford_Quays" title="Salford Quays">Salford Quays</a> (Marks &amp; Spencer Shared Services Ltd. which provides human resources, and finance administration)<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Chester" title="Chester">Chester</a> (HSBC's M&amp;S Money and Retail Customer Services).<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The company has overseas sourcing offices in Malaysia, Hong Kong, Thailand, India, Bangladesh, Turkey, China, Italy, Indonesia and Sri Lanka.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_performance">Financial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Financial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</p>
