<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_and_environmental_policy">Social and environmental policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Social and environmental policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id=".22Look_Behind_the_Label.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Look_Behind_the_Label&quot;">"Look Behind the Label"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: &quot;Look Behind the Label&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2006, the <i>Look Behind the Label</i> marketing campaign was introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The aim of this campaign was to highlight to customers the various ethical and environmentally friendly aspects of the production and sourcing methods engaged in by M&amp;S including: <a href="/wiki/Fairtrade" class="mw-redirect" title="Fairtrade">Fairtrade</a> products, <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_fishing" class="mw-redirect" title="Sustainable fishing">sustainable fishing</a> and environmentally friendly textile dyes. All coffee and tea sold in M&amp;S stores is now Fairtrade.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the company offers clothing lines made from Fairtrade cotton in selected departments.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At Christmas, the company introduces a range of food products to support the housing charity <a href="/wiki/Shelter_(charity)" title="Shelter (charity)">Shelter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MarksAndSpencerBirmingham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/MarksAndSpencerBirmingham.jpg/220px-MarksAndSpencerBirmingham.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/MarksAndSpencerBirmingham.jpg/330px-MarksAndSpencerBirmingham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/MarksAndSpencerBirmingham.jpg/440px-MarksAndSpencerBirmingham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MarksAndSpencerBirmingham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>M&amp;S store on <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> High Street</div></div></div>
<p>On 15 January 2007, M&amp;S launched an initiative, known as "Plan A",<sup id="cite_ref-PlanA_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PlanA-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> to dramatically increase the environmental <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a> of the business within 5 years and expected to cost £200&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The plan covers "100 commitments over 5 years to address the key social and environmental challenges facing M&amp;S today and in the future" with the tag-line "Because there is no Plan B". The commitments span five themes: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waste" title="Waste">waste</a>, sustainable raw materials, 'fair partnership' and health,<sup id="cite_ref-PlanA_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PlanA-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> with the aim that, by 2012, it will:<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Become carbon neutral</li>
<li>Send no waste to landfill</li>
<li>Extend sustainable sourcing</li>
<li>Help improve the lives of people in their supply chain</li>
<li>Help customers and employees live a healthier life-style</li></ul>
<p>Despite an 18% fall in the share price in January 2008, following publication of their latest <a href="/wiki/Trading_statement" title="Trading statement">trading statement</a>, the company confirmed that they would be continuing with the plan, saying that there were 'compelling commercial&#160;— as well as moral&#160;— reasons to do so'.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>M&amp;S introduced a reusable <a href="/wiki/Hessian_(cloth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hessian (cloth)">hessian</a> bag in 2007 as part of the plan, aiming to reduce the number of plastic bags used within five years. This was followed in May 2008 by the introduction of a 5p charge for standard sized carrier bags used for food purchases (before this charge became compulsory).<sup id="cite_ref-PlanA_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PlanA-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> All profits from the sale of food bags originally went to the charity <a href="/wiki/Groundwork_UK" title="Groundwork UK">Groundwork UK</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> M&amp;S launched the "Forever Fish" campaign in June 2011 and switched funding to that campaign to promote protection of marine wildlife in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In becoming carbon neutral the company has committed to only use <a href="/wiki/Carbon_offset" title="Carbon offset">carbon offsetting</a> as a last resort,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> restricted to cases "where it is required by government or where the technology for green air or road transport will not be available for the foreseeable future".<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of August 2008, M&amp;S had three <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbines" class="mw-redirect" title="Wind turbines">wind turbines</a> in operation, one at <a href="/wiki/Methlick" title="Methlick">Methlick</a> and two near <a href="/wiki/Strichen" title="Strichen">Strichen</a>, generating enough power to supply three stores via the <a href="/wiki/National_Grid_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Grid (UK)">National Grid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In April 2009 the company began purchasing 2.6&#160;<a href="/wiki/TWh" class="mw-redirect" title="TWh">TWh</a> of renewable energy (wind and hydroelectric) from <a href="/wiki/Npower_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Npower (UK)">Npower</a>, enough to power all Marks &amp; Spencer stores and offices in England and Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012 the company was awarded <a href="/wiki/European_Business_Awards_for_the_Environment" title="European Business Awards for the Environment">European Business Award for the Environment</a> (Management category) by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> for Plan A.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_work">Charity work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Charity work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>M&amp;S has sold a wide range of charitable women's clothes for <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Breast_Cancer" title="Breakthrough Breast Cancer">Breakthrough Breast Cancer</a><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> for many years and the <a href="/wiki/Ashbourne,_Derbyshire" title="Ashbourne, Derbyshire">Ashbourne</a> store collected a total of £2,000 for a local <a href="/wiki/Derbyshire" title="Derbyshire">Derbyshire</a> hospital's new ECG machine in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In 2011 M&amp;S launch <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a>'s clothes recycling initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior_management">Senior management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Senior management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following have served as the Chairman of the company since it was founded:
</p>
<ul><li>1884–1907: <a href="/wiki/Michael_Marks" title="Michael Marks">Michael Marks</a> (set up first stall in Leeds in 1884)</li>
<li>1907–1916: William Chapman.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1916–1964: <a href="/wiki/Simon_Marks" class="mw-redirect" title="Simon Marks">Simon Marks</a> (Lord Marks)</li>
<li>1964–1967: <a href="/wiki/Israel_Sieff" class="mw-redirect" title="Israel Sieff">Israel Sieff</a> (Lord Sieff)</li>
<li>1967–1972: <a href="/wiki/Edward_Sieff" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward Sieff">Edward Sieff</a></li>
<li>1972–1984: <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Sieff" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcus Sieff">Marcus Sieff</a> (Lord Sieff)</li>
<li>1984–1991: <a href="/wiki/Derek_Rayner,_Baron_Rayner" title="Derek Rayner, Baron Rayner">Derek Rayner</a> (Lord Rayner)</li>
<li>1991–1999: <a href="/wiki/Richard_Greenbury" title="Richard Greenbury">Sir Richard Greenbury</a></li>
<li>2000–2004: Luc Vandevelde</li>
<li>2004–2006: <a href="/wiki/Paul_Myners" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul Myners">Paul Myners</a></li>
<li>2006–2009: <a href="/wiki/Terence_Burns,_Baron_Burns" title="Terence Burns, Baron Burns">Lord Burns</a></li>
<li>2009–2010: <a href="/wiki/Sir_Stuart_Rose" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Stuart Rose">Sir Stuart Rose</a></li>
<li>2011–2017: <a href="/wiki/Robert_Swannell" title="Robert Swannell">Robert Swannell</a></li>
<li>2017–present: <a href="/wiki/Archie_Norman" title="Archie Norman">Archie Norman</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stores">Stores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Stores">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UK_and_Ireland">UK and Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: UK and Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_picture_of_M%26S_White_City_branch_in_Westfield_London_2014-01-17_17-26.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/A_picture_of_M%26S_White_City_branch_in_Westfield_London_2014-01-17_17-26.jpg/220px-A_picture_of_M%26S_White_City_branch_in_Westfield_London_2014-01-17_17-26.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/A_picture_of_M%26S_White_City_branch_in_Westfield_London_2014-01-17_17-26.jpg/330px-A_picture_of_M%26S_White_City_branch_in_Westfield_London_2014-01-17_17-26.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/A_picture_of_M%26S_White_City_branch_in_Westfield_London_2014-01-17_17-26.jpg/440px-A_picture_of_M%26S_White_City_branch_in_Westfield_London_2014-01-17_17-26.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_picture_of_M%26S_White_City_branch_in_Westfield_London_2014-01-17_17-26.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>M&amp;S White City in <a href="/wiki/Westfield_London" title="Westfield London">Westfield London</a> (2014) is one of the company's largest stores.</div></div></div>
<p>The largest shop is at <a href="/wiki/Marble_Arch" title="Marble Arch">Marble Arch</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Street" title="Oxford Street">Oxford Street</a> in London, which has around 16,000 square metres (170,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) of <a href="/wiki/Shop_floor" title="Shop floor">shop floor</a>. The second largest is in Cheshire Oaks, <a href="/wiki/Ellesmere_Port" title="Ellesmere Port">Ellesmere Port</a>, which is the largest outside London.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The third largest shop is at the Gemini Retail Park in <a href="/wiki/Warrington" title="Warrington">Warrington</a>. In 1999 M&amp;S opened its shop in <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Exchange_Square_(Manchester)" class="mw-redirect" title="Exchange Square (Manchester)">Exchange Square</a>, which was destroyed in the <a href="/wiki/1996_Manchester_bombing" title="1996 Manchester bombing">1996 Manchester bombing</a> and rebuilt. At re-opening, it was the largest M&amp;S shop with 23,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (250,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) of retail space, but half was subsequently sold to <a href="/wiki/Selfridges" title="Selfridges">Selfridges</a>, the company's second site in Manchester.  The smallest branch is a 'Marks &amp; Spencer Penny Bazaar' clearance outlet located in the <a href="/wiki/Grainger_Market" class="mw-redirect" title="Grainger Market">Grainger Market</a> in Newcastle upon Tyne.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>M&amp;S has opened a number of stores at out of town locations since the trend to build shopping centres away from town centres became popular in the 1980s. The first was at the <a href="/wiki/MetroCentre_(shopping_centre)" title="MetroCentre (shopping centre)">MetroCentre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" title="Gateshead">Gateshead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear" title="Tyne and Wear">Tyne and Wear</a>, which opened in 1986. Another notable example is the store at the <a href="/wiki/Merry_Hill_Shopping_Centre" title="Merry Hill Shopping Centre">Merry Hill Shopping Centre</a> at <a href="/wiki/Brierley_Hill" title="Brierley Hill">Brierley Hill</a>, West Midlands. This store opened on 23 October 1990 shortly after the closure of stores in the nearby town centres of <a href="/wiki/Dudley" title="Dudley">Dudley</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich" title="West Bromwich">West Bromwich</a>; the Merry Hill store was not originally intended to replace these two town centre stores, but both the Dudley and West Bromwich stores had experienced a downturn in trade as the opening of the Merry Hill store loomed, and both stores were closed on 25 August 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before Christmas 2006, twenty-two M&amp;S shops were open for 24-hour trading including stores at <a href="/wiki/Bolton" title="Bolton">Bolton</a> Middlebrook and at the Abbey Centre, <a href="/wiki/Newtownabbey" title="Newtownabbey">Newtownabbey</a>, Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The company's website has received criticism for having its prices in <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">Pound sterling</a> and not in euro, and for providing a search for its Irish stores through a "UK Store Finder".<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Irish_Times" title="The Irish Times">The Irish Times</a></i> pointed out that M&amp;S failed to explain why the company is in a position to deliver goods ordered from its website to Brazil, Argentina, Iraq and Afghanistan but not to Ireland. M&amp;S did not comment.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_%26_Spencer,_The_Mall_Athens.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_The_Mall_Athens.JPG/220px-Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_The_Mall_Athens.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_The_Mall_Athens.JPG/330px-Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_The_Mall_Athens.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_The_Mall_Athens.JPG/440px-Marks_%26_Spencer%2C_The_Mall_Athens.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_%26_Spencer,_The_Mall_Athens.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Marks &amp; Spencer branch in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a></div></div></div>
<p>The company reopened its store in Paris on 24 November 2011, following the launch of a new French website on 11 October 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In the Philippines there are 18 M&amp;S shops, the largest of which is located in <a href="/wiki/Greenbelt_(Ayala_Center)" title="Greenbelt (Ayala Center)">Greenbelt Mall</a>. A new store opened on 17 April 2013 in <a href="/wiki/Kalverstraat" title="Kalverstraat">Kalverstraat</a> in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, more than 10 years after closure of the previous store. On 17 September 2013 the British ambassador to the Netherlands, Sir Geoffrey Adams, opened the first Dutch Marks &amp; Spencer Food pilot store at a BP petrol station in Bijleveld beside the A12 motorway.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> There are over 300 stores in some 40 overseas locations.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 November 2013, Marks &amp; Spencer announced "that it is set to have about 80 stores open in the region by 2016 as part of its strategy to become a leading international, multichannel retailer" with partner Reliance Retail.<sup id="cite_ref-Marks_&amp;_Spencer_to_Expand_in_India_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marks_&amp;_Spencer_to_Expand_in_India-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> It opened a flagship store in Bandra in Mumbai.<sup id="cite_ref-Marks_&amp;_Spencer_to_Expand_in_India_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marks_&amp;_Spencer_to_Expand_in_India-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> M&amp;S sales of lingerie accounts for more than a fifth of the sales in the Indian market, with total lingerie sales increasing by a third during the last six months of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Marks_&amp;_Spencer_to_Expand_in_India_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marks_&amp;_Spencer_to_Expand_in_India-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>  In May 2014 Marks &amp; Spencer announced that their intention was now to open 100 stores in the country by 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the Netherlands, as of 2015, M&amp;S have a supermarket in the expensive <a href="/wiki/Kalverstraat" title="Kalverstraat">Kalverstraat</a> shopping street in Amsterdam, as well as a larger store including clothing in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>. A number of <a href="/wiki/British_Petroleum" class="mw-redirect" title="British Petroleum">BP</a> petrol stations in the Western area of the Netherlands include M&amp;S <a href="/wiki/Convenience_food" title="Convenience food">convenience food</a> stores.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, M&amp;S is due to open a much larger store in Amsterdam, with a direct underground link to a new metro station.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Store_formats">Store formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Store formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Full_line_stores">Full line stores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Full line stores">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_and_Spencer.Kirkcaldy.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Marks_and_Spencer.Kirkcaldy.JPG/220px-Marks_and_Spencer.Kirkcaldy.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Marks_and_Spencer.Kirkcaldy.JPG/330px-Marks_and_Spencer.Kirkcaldy.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Marks_and_Spencer.Kirkcaldy.JPG/440px-Marks_and_Spencer.Kirkcaldy.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_and_Spencer.Kirkcaldy.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A typical example of an un-modernised 'core' M&amp;S store, located in <a href="/wiki/Kirkcaldy" title="Kirkcaldy">Kirkcaldy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fife" title="Fife">Fife</a>. However, as of 2012 the store has now been fully refurbished with the so-called "Light Touch" re-fit.</div></div></div>
<p>M&amp;S core shops typically feature a selection of the company's clothing, homeware and beauty ranges and an M&amp;S <a href="/wiki/Food_hall" title="Food hall">FOODHALL</a> The range of clothing sold and the space given to it depends on the location and customer demographic (an example would be that some London shops do not stock the Classic Collection, but stock Limited Edition and a full Autograph range). All full line shops feature a Food hall. The current store format was designed by Urban Salon Architects in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Foodhall_.28in-store.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Foodhall_(in-store)">Foodhall (in-store)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Foodhall (in-store)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M%26S_Food_Hall,_SUTTON,_Surrey,_Greater_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/M%26S_Food_Hall%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg/220px-M%26S_Food_Hall%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/M%26S_Food_Hall%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg/330px-M%26S_Food_Hall%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/M%26S_Food_Hall%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg/440px-M%26S_Food_Hall%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3957" data-file-height="2502" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M%26S_Food_Hall,_SUTTON,_Surrey,_Greater_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An M&amp;S Food Hall in the <a href="/wiki/Sutton,_London" title="Sutton, London">Sutton, London</a> branch</div></div></div>
<p>All the <b>St Michael Food hall</b> supermarkets were renamed <i>M&amp;S Food hall</i> when Marks &amp; Spencer dropped the <i>St Michael</i> brand in 2000. Each M&amp;S Foodhall sells groceries, which are all under the Marks &amp; Spencer brand. However, in 2009 the company began selling a limited range of other brands, such as <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stella_Artois" title="Stella Artois">Stella Artois</a>, without reducing the number of M&amp;S goods they sold. This marked the first time in its 125-year history that Marks &amp; Spencer had sold any brands other than its own.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>M&amp;S introduced <a href="/wiki/Self_check-out" class="mw-redirect" title="Self check-out">self check-out</a> tills in the food-halls of a small number of trial stores in 2002. Self check-out was implemented in the general merchandise sections in three trial stores in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hospitality">Hospitality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Hospitality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many large shops, such as Lisburn Sprucefield, <a href="/wiki/Westfield_London" title="Westfield London">Westfield, White City</a>, Cribbs Causeway and <a href="/wiki/Newcastle-upon-Tyne" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle-upon-Tyne">Newcastle-upon-Tyne</a>, also offer other hospitality outlets, such as a modern <i>Deli Bar</i> (champagne, canapés, seafood), <i>Restaurant</i> (table service—the first of which was opened in Newcastle) <i>M&amp;S Kitchen</i> (traditional home cooking &amp; lunches) or <i>Hot Food To Go</i> (burgers, chips, soups).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_stores">Home stores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Home stores">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2007, M&amp;S announced that new, dedicated shops for home furnishings were to be launched. Shops have now been opened in <a href="/wiki/Cheltenham" title="Cheltenham">Cheltenham</a> in Gloucestershire, <a href="/wiki/Tunbridge_Wells" class="mw-redirect" title="Tunbridge Wells">Tunbridge Wells</a> in Kent, <a href="/wiki/Lisburn" title="Lisburn">Lisburn</a> Sprucefield in Northern Ireland<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and in the Barton Square section of <a href="/wiki/Trafford_Centre" title="Trafford Centre">The Trafford Centre</a>, Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Outlet_stores">Outlet stores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Outlet stores">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>M&amp;S have 30 outlet stores. The outlet division offers M&amp;S products with the majority of them discounting at least 30% from the original selling price.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The first of these stores opened at <a href="/wiki/Ashford,_Kent" title="Ashford, Kent">Ashford</a> in Kent in 2000. Many of the Outlet shops are in locations such as retail parks and outlet centres, though some, including the shop in <a href="/wiki/Woolwich" title="Woolwich">Woolwich</a>, South London.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="M.26S_Foodhall_.28standalone.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="M&amp;S_Foodhall_(standalone)">M&amp;S Foodhall (standalone)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: M&amp;S Foodhall (standalone)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_and_Spencer,_Banstead,_Surrey_-_geograph.org.uk_-_339773.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Marks_and_Spencer%2C_Banstead%2C_Surrey_-_geograph.org.uk_-_339773.jpg/220px-Marks_and_Spencer%2C_Banstead%2C_Surrey_-_geograph.org.uk_-_339773.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Marks_and_Spencer%2C_Banstead%2C_Surrey_-_geograph.org.uk_-_339773.jpg/330px-Marks_and_Spencer%2C_Banstead%2C_Surrey_-_geograph.org.uk_-_339773.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Marks_and_Spencer%2C_Banstead%2C_Surrey_-_geograph.org.uk_-_339773.jpg/440px-Marks_and_Spencer%2C_Banstead%2C_Surrey_-_geograph.org.uk_-_339773.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_and_Spencer,_Banstead,_Surrey_-_geograph.org.uk_-_339773.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>M&amp;S Simply Food in <a href="/wiki/Banstead" title="Banstead">Banstead</a>, Surrey</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M%26S_Food_to_Go,_SUTTON,_Surrey,_Greater_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/M%26S_Food_to_Go%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg/220px-M%26S_Food_to_Go%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/M%26S_Food_to_Go%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg/330px-M%26S_Food_to_Go%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/M%26S_Food_to_Go%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg/440px-M%26S_Food_to_Go%2C_SUTTON%2C_Surrey%2C_Greater_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M%26S_Food_to_Go,_SUTTON,_Surrey,_Greater_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An M&amp;S Food to Go store in Sutton station, <a href="/wiki/Sutton,_London" title="Sutton, London">Sutton, London</a></div></div></div>
<p>M&amp;S launched a convenience format, branded <i>Simply Food</i> in 2001, with the first stores opening in <a href="/wiki/Twickenham" title="Twickenham">Twickenham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surbiton" title="Surbiton">Surbiton</a>. The stores predominantly sell food, however some larger stores also stock a small selection of general merchandise.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of these are run under <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchise</a> agreements:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/SSP_Group" title="SSP Group">SSP Group</a> runs the stores at mainline railway stations and airports.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Moto_Hospitality" title="Moto Hospitality">Moto</a> has stores at 45 of its motorway service stations.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a> has over 120 petrol stations with <i>Simply Food</i> offerings.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Orders from M&amp;S accounted for more than half of <a href="/wiki/Uniq_plc" title="Uniq plc">Uniq</a>'s food product supplies to UK retailers in 2010 after several years service as a major M&amp;S food product supplier.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011 it was noted that M&amp;S were operating <a href="/wiki/Express_pricing" title="Express pricing">express pricing</a>; i.e., charging more in their Simply Food branches than in regular branches. A spokesperson stated that "prices are a little higher than at our high street stores but this reflects the fact that these stores are open longer and are highly convenient for customers on the move".<sup id="cite_ref-m&amp;s_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m&amp;s-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Simply Food brand has been phased out in all stand-alone larger stores since the rebrand in 2015 and the stores have now been branded as "M&amp;S Foodhall."<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2019 M&amp;S announced that they would open more supermarket sized food halls (between 10,000 and 15,000 sq ft.) that would stock their full food range in order to attract more families looking to do a weekly shop. M&amp;S have also lowered the price of over 1000 of their popular lines to compete with their larger supermarket rivals such as Tesco and Sainsbury’s.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_services">Online services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Online services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Products could be ordered online since the mid-2000s, in response to <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a> launching their pioneering <a href="/wiki/Tesco.com" title="Tesco.com">Tesco.com</a> home shopping delivery service in the early 2000s. Both Tesco, M&amp;S and others are expanding rapidly into this new niche market.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The online flower service was accused of unfair trading and using <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> to piggy-back advertise on online searches aimed at <a href="/wiki/Interflora" title="Interflora">Interflora</a> online in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/John_Lewis_(department_store)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Lewis (department store)">John Lewis</a> shopping chain beat M&amp;S to the title of the UK's best high-street website by late 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Product_line_history">Product line history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Product line history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Marks_%26_Spencer_brands" title="List of Marks &amp; Spencer brands">List of Marks &amp; Spencer brands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Women_peruna.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/39/Women_peruna.jpg/220px-Women_peruna.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="82" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/39/Women_peruna.jpg/330px-Women_peruna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/39/Women_peruna.jpg 2x" data-file-width="343" data-file-height="128" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Women_peruna.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Per Una's logo, three hearts</div></div></div>
<p>The "St Michael" brand was introduced by Simon Marks in 1928 in honour of his father and co-founder of Marks &amp; Spencer, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Marks" title="Michael Marks">Michael Marks</a>. By 1950, virtually all goods were sold under the St Michael brand. M&amp;S lingerie, women's clothing and girls' uniform were branded under the <i>St Margaret</i> brand, until the whole range of general merchandise became St Michael.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Marks &amp; Spencer were selling clothes under the <i>St Margaret</i> and <i>St Michael</i> label by the mid-1950s and launched their <a href="/wiki/School_uniforms" class="mw-redirect" title="School uniforms">school uniforms</a> in the early 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The synthetic fibre Tricell was first used in 1957 and lasted until the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and another synthetic fibre called Courtelle was first launched, nationally, by Marks &amp; Spencer during 1960 and also lasted well into the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Machine washable wool first appeared in 1972 and <a href="/wiki/Lycra" class="mw-redirect" title="Lycra">Lycra</a> hosiery first came in during 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>"Per Una" was launched on 28 September 2001 as a joint venture between M&amp;S and <a href="/wiki/Next_plc" title="Next plc">Next</a> founder <a href="/wiki/George_Davies_(retailer)" title="George Davies (retailer)">George Davies</a> with the contribution of Julie Strang. The <i>Per Una</i> brand has been a major success for the company,<sup id="cite_ref-davies_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-davies-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> and in October 2004, M&amp;S bought the brand in a £125&#160;million, two-year service contract with George Davies.<sup id="cite_ref-per_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-per-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Mr Davies was to stay on for at least two years to run the company, with 12 months notice required if he wished to leave.<sup id="cite_ref-davies_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-davies-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-per_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-per-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, Sir Stuart Rose axed a number of brands including the menswear brand "SP Clothing", the "View From" sportswear range, the <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> children's range "DB07" and several food lines as he thought the company's stock inventory management had become 'too complicated'.<sup id="cite_ref-thisismoney.co.uk_512068_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thisismoney.co.uk_512068-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> A version of Per Una aimed at teenagers, "Per Una Due", was also discontinued, despite having launched earlier in the year, due to poor sales.<sup id="cite_ref-thisismoney.co.uk_512068_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thisismoney.co.uk_512068-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The company also began to sell branded goods like <a href="/wiki/Kellogg%27s_Corn_Flakes" class="mw-redirect" title="Kellogg&#39;s Corn Flakes">Kellogg's Corn Flakes</a> in November 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-top_brands_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top_brands-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Following a review by Marc Bolland in 2011, M&amp;S confirmed it would begin to reduce the number of branded items on sale, instead offering only those that it did not have an M&amp;S alternative for.<sup id="cite_ref-ausfoodnews.com.au_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ausfoodnews.com.au-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_logo">New logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: New logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_%26_Spencer_corporate_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Marks_%26_Spencer_corporate_logo.svg/220px-Marks_%26_Spencer_corporate_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="83" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Marks_%26_Spencer_corporate_logo.svg/330px-Marks_%26_Spencer_corporate_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Marks_%26_Spencer_corporate_logo.svg/440px-Marks_%26_Spencer_corporate_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="151" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_%26_Spencer_corporate_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The older logo, used from 2000 to 2007</div></div></div>
<p>During the height of the company's troubles at the beginning of the 21st century, the <i>St Michael</i> brand used as the selling label for all M&amp;S products was discontinued in favour of <i>Marks &amp; Spencer</i> and a new logo in the <a href="/wiki/Optima" title="Optima">Optima</a> typeface was introduced and began to appear in place of <i>St Michael</i> on product packaging. The same logo was also applied to store fascias and carrier bags. The <i>St Michael</i> name was subsequently adopted as a 'quality guarantee' and appeared as the <i>St Michael Quality Promise</i> on the back of food products, on the side of delivery vehicles and on in-store ordering receipts.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Your_M.26S"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Your_M&amp;S">Your M&amp;S</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Your M&amp;S">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Your_M%26S_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Your_M%26S_logo.svg/220px-Your_M%26S_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="78" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Your_M%26S_logo.svg/330px-Your_M%26S_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Your_M%26S_logo.svg/440px-Your_M%26S_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="340" data-file-height="120" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Your_M%26S_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Your M&amp;S</i> promotional logo 2004–2014.</div></div></div>
<p>When Steve Sharp joined as marketing director in 2004, after being hired by new Chief Executive Sir Stuart Rose, he introduced a new promotional brand under the <i>Your M&amp;S</i> banner, with a corresponding logo.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High-profile_media_campaigns">High-profile media campaigns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: High-profile media campaigns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_%26_Spencer_new_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Marks_%26_Spencer_new_logo.svg/220px-Marks_%26_Spencer_new_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="87" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Marks_%26_Spencer_new_logo.svg/330px-Marks_%26_Spencer_new_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Marks_%26_Spencer_new_logo.svg/440px-Marks_%26_Spencer_new_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="371" data-file-height="146" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marks_%26_Spencer_new_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo 2007-2015</div></div></div>
<p>M&amp;S has always run newspaper and/or Magazine advertisements since the early 1950s, but the introduction of some famous stars such as <a href="/wiki/Twiggy" title="Twiggy">Twiggy</a><sup id="cite_ref-telegraph1_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph1-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/David_Jason" title="David Jason">David Jason</a> in various TV ads has helped raise the company's profile. Twiggy first appeared in 1967, returning later in 1995 and 2005. Anne Grierson<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> first featured in advertisements during the late 1950s and most of the 1960s. In later years, <a href="/wiki/Erin_O%27Connor" title="Erin O&#39;Connor">Erin O'Connor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph1_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph1-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Myleene_Klass" title="Myleene Klass">Myleene Klass</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph1_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph1-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Tanja Nadjila, Peter Kay, <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Banderas" title="Antonio Banderas">Antonio Banderas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Claudia_Schiffer" title="Claudia Schiffer">Claudia Schiffer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Helena_Christensen" title="Helena Christensen">Helena Christensen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tatjana_Patitz" title="Tatjana Patitz">Tatjana Patitz</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Snowdon" title="Lisa Snowdon">Lisa Snowdon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dannii_Minogue" title="Dannii Minogue">Dannii Minogue</a>, <a href="/wiki/V_V_Brown" title="V V Brown">V V Brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Kass" title="Carmen Kass">Carmen Kass</a> have also featured in a few advertisements, along with many others.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Sergeant_(journalist)" title="John Sergeant (journalist)">John Sergeant</a>, David Jason and <a href="/wiki/Joanna_Lumley" title="Joanna Lumley">Joanna Lumley</a> have either appeared in or voiced over advertisements since 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-marksintime_13-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksintime-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The new look has been instrumental in the company's recent resurgence, particularly with the success of a new clothing campaign featuring the celebrated model, <a href="/wiki/Twiggy" title="Twiggy">Twiggy</a>, and younger models associated with the <a href="/wiki/Boho-chic#The_influence_of_boho" title="Boho-chic">bohemian</a> styles of 2005–6, and the new TV ad campaign for its food range. These advertisements have the tag-line "This is not just food, this is M&amp;S food" and feature slow motion, close-up footage of various food products, described in a sultry <a href="/wiki/Voice-over" title="Voice-over">voice-over</a> by <a href="/wiki/Dervla_Kirwan" title="Dervla Kirwan">Dervla Kirwan</a>, to an enticing instrumental song&#160;— including Fleetwood Mac's "<a href="/wiki/Albatross_(instrumental)" title="Albatross (instrumental)">Albatross</a>" as well as <a href="/wiki/Santana_(band)" title="Santana (band)">Santana</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Samba_Pa_Ti_(instrumental)" title="Samba Pa Ti (instrumental)">Samba Pa Ti</a>", <a href="/wiki/Olly_Murs" title="Olly Murs">Olly Murs</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Busy_(Olly_Murs_song)" title="Busy (Olly Murs song)">Busy</a>", <a href="/wiki/Groove_Armada" title="Groove Armada">Groove Armada</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/At_the_River" title="At the River">At the River</a>" or <a href="/wiki/Spandau_Ballet" title="Spandau Ballet">Spandau Ballet</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/True_(Spandau_Ballet_song)" title="True (Spandau Ballet song)">True</a>". These advertisements have been referred to by both fans and critics as being <i><a href="/wiki/Food_porn" title="Food porn">food porn</a></i>, with a number of other companies copying the idea, such as <a href="/wiki/Aldi" title="Aldi">Aldi</a> and, subsequently, <a href="/wiki/Waitrose" class="mw-redirect" title="Waitrose">Waitrose</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2009 TV advertising campaign drew complaints, leading to national press coverage, regarding sexism.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, it was confirmed that Dannii Minogue would be one of the new faces of Marks &amp; Spencer. She filmed her first commercial in South Africa, which featured <a href="/wiki/Cheryl_Lynn" title="Cheryl Lynn">Cheryl Lynn</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Got_to_Be_Real" title="Got to Be Real">Got to Be Real</a>", for their Spring campaign that aired on 24 March.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Dannii travelled to <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, Florida in January 2011 to shoot the commercial for M&amp;S for the 2011 Spring collection, prior to her contractual termination. In August 2011, M&amp;S announced the new faces of their campaigns would be <a href="/wiki/Rosie_Huntington-Whiteley" title="Rosie Huntington-Whiteley">Rosie Huntington-Whiteley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Reynolds" title="Ryan Reynolds">Ryan Reynolds</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Gandy" title="David Gandy">David Gandy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Marks &amp; Spencer dropped a series of planned television adverts in the July 2011, featuring <a href="/wiki/Twiggy" title="Twiggy">Twiggy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dannii_Minogue" title="Dannii Minogue">Dannii Minogue</a> and <a href="/wiki/VV_Brown" class="mw-redirect" title="VV Brown">VV Brown</a>  as it started its corporate image revamp. It confirmed that Twiggy, <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Snowden" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisa Snowden">Lisa Snowden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Redknapp" title="Jamie Redknapp">Jamie Redknapp</a> would return for future advertising.<sup id="cite_ref-peacock1_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peacock1-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 31 March 2014, M&amp;S launched the new iteration of its 'Leading Ladies' marketing campaign featuring figures including <a href="/wiki/Emma_Thompson" title="Emma Thompson">Emma Thompson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annie_Lennox" title="Annie Lennox">Annie Lennox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rita_Ora" title="Rita Ora">Rita Ora</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baroness_Lawrence" class="mw-redirect" title="Baroness Lawrence">Baroness Lawrence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-Israel_protests">Anti-Israel protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Anti-Israel protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Due to a mistaken belief that the store is owned by Jews,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Marks &amp; Spencer has been repeatedly targeted and boycotted by anti-Israel protestors, both during the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League_boycott_of_Israel" title="Arab League boycott of Israel">Arab League boycott of Israel</a><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> and  the more recent <a href="/wiki/Boycott,_Divestment_and_Sanctions" title="Boycott, Divestment and Sanctions">Boycott, Divestment and Sanctions</a> (BDS) movement. In 2014, it was reported that the Marble Arch branch was picketed weekly by BDS sympathizers.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Comprehensive_Spending_Review">Comprehensive Spending Review</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Comprehensive Spending Review">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/2010_Spending_Review" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 Spending Review">2010 Spending Review</a></div>
<p>In October 2010, chairman Sir Stuart Rose was a signatory to a controversial letter to <i>The Daily Telegraph</i><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> which claimed that "The private sector should be more than capable of generating additional jobs to replace those lost in the public sector, and the redeployment of people to more productive activities will improve economic performance, so generating more employment opportunities", despite recent job cuts of 1,000 staff.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> This prompted calls for a boycott of Marks &amp; Spencer and the companies represented by the other signatories to the letter.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Contactless_payment_issues">Contactless payment issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Contactless payment issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Some Marks &amp; Spencer customers claim that the chain's <a href="/wiki/Contactless_payment" title="Contactless payment">contactless payment</a> terminals have taken money from cards other than the ones intended for payment. Contactless cards are supposed to be within about 4&#160;cm of the front of the terminal to work. M&amp;S investigated the incident and confirmed the new system had been extensively tested and was robust. It had recently rolled out the contactless payments system, provided by Visa Europe, to 644 UK stores.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Muslim_checkout-staff_policy">Muslim checkout-staff policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Muslim checkout-staff policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In December 2013, Marks &amp; Spencer announced that Muslim checkout staff in the UK could refuse to sell pork products or alcohol to customers at their till.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The policy was announced after at least one news outlet reported that customers waiting with goods that included pork or alcohol were refused service, and were told by a Muslim checkout worker to wait until another till became available.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The policy applied across all 703 UK M&amp;S stores and prompted a strong backlash by customers.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A company spokesman subsequently apologised and stated that they will attempt to reassign staff whose beliefs may impact their work to different departments, such as clothing.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hijab_as_school_uniform">Hijab as school uniform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Hijab as school uniform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Marks &amp; Spencer introduced a hijab in its section of school uniforms in late 2018 and subsequently faced backlash and boycott from customers; the product is stocked for girls as young as three.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Holly_Willoughby">Holly Willoughby</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Holly Willoughby">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In September 2018, <a href="/wiki/Holly_Willoughby" title="Holly Willoughby">Holly Willoughby</a> became the company new brand ambassador along with her 'Must Have' collection which launched on 27 September 2018. However the company failed to order sufficient stock and large quantities of customers were left disappointed.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marks_%26_Spencer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
